* <2026-03-30 Mon>

*Zonal Engagement*

Dropping other work now, on Joe's request, to focus fully on Zonal. We're consulting with Zonal, a pub/restaurant software company (~1,700 sites). The engagement splits into: (1) maintaining their legacy stack (core revenue, runs on-site hardware, high key-person risk), (2) modernising it (framework upgrades, security, UI refreshes), (3) picking up the stalled Zonal Connect replatform (mobile-first, repos gone quiet since contractors left), and optionally (4) an SLM skunkworks idea of Ian's (only if Adam/Glenn at Zonal show they get the vision). Leadership want 6–8 weeks max, coaching not doing. There's also an accelerator workshop: days 1–2 foundational AI, days 3–4 team-based builds across those areas.

My focus is the legacy stack — dig into the repos, assess CI/CD, deployments, monitoring, logging, code health. If it's generally tight, pivot to showing them AI patterns (debugging, log analysis, doc generation). Flag anything that'd work as a 20–30 min accelerator exercise. Kaushal is on similar ground but leaning modernisation; Chris Laidler is on Zonal Connect. Key contacts at Zonal: Adam (product director / future eng lead) and Glenn (head of product).

- [ ] Dig into Zonal legacy repos this week — look for improvements, risks, and training material
- [ ] Prepare questions for the Wed demo call with Zonal

- [ ] Book holiday for Thursday afternoon (2026-04-02) via Workday — system expected back online Tue/Wed

    **Bug-first evidence:** added API regression for retry path where previously received line items cause `exceeds_outstanding_quantity` (`line item ... has only 0 outstanding units`) and block remaining line items; test fails on current branch before fix.
    **Fix implemented:** `receive-order-complete` now treats retry payload items idempotently by skipping line items already fully received and clamping previously-partial line items to current outstanding quantity, so remaining items still complete.
    **Validation (targeted):** `bun --cwd tests/api test orders/large-order-receive.test.ts -t "treats retry payload items with zero outstanding quantity as idempotent and completes remaining items"` (**fails before fix, passes after**); `bun --cwd containers/actions-api test src/routes/receive-order-complete.test.ts` (**pass**); `bun --cwd tests/api test orders/large-order-receive.test.ts` (**3 tests passing**).
  - [X] https://e-isg.visualstudio.com/eQuip%20USASOC/_workitems/edit/28836 (transaction completion report)
    **PR plan:** reports PR only if report-side root cause; otherwise standalone.
    **In Develop (Codex, 2026-03-03):** set WI `28836` to `Active` (assigned to Rob Kirby), then `In Develop` once PR opened; branched `codex/28836-transaction-completion-report` from latest `origin/develop` (`24a3b9621`).
    **Root cause:** `/api/v1/transactions/latest` was returning `createdAt` from `asset_transaction` rows, which are created at completion time; the Transaction Completion Report elapsed math (`processedAt - createdAt`) therefore collapsed to `00:00:00`.
    **Fix implemented:** enriched `/api/v1/transactions/latest` response rows with parent `transaction` timestamps/actors (`createdAt`, `updatedAt`, `createdBy`, `updatedBy`) plus parent `date_processed`, with fallback to existing asset-transaction fields if parent lookup is unavailable.
    **Follow-up fix (Codex, 2026-03-03):** after user repro (`Internal Server Error`), added proof-first failing API test for transaction-completion report generation and fixed a regression in the new summary query (`api_v1.entities` does not expose `created_by`/`updated_by`); summary select now requests only existing columns and non-UUID `transaction_id` values are skipped for summary lookup.
    **PR opened:** [[https://e-isg.visualstudio.com/eQuip%20USASOC/_git/eQuip%20USASOC/pullrequest/1088][1088]] (`WI 28836: fix transaction completion elapsed time source`) linked to WI `28836`.
    **Validation (targeted):** `bun --cwd containers/actions-api test src/routes/transactions.test.ts` => **1 file, 20 tests passing**; `bun --cwd tests/api test reports/report-generation.test.ts -t "transaction-completion report generates for a bounded date range"` => **pass**.
  - [X] https://e-isg.visualstudio.com/eQuip%20USASOC/_workitems/edit/28833 (cleared service member report)

  **Plain-English summary of what this PR changes now:**
  - Adds a shared RBAC policy layer in web + actions-api that reads CIAM/Keycloak roles, normalizes aliases, and enforces visitor precedence (visitor overrides elevated roles if both appear).
  - Gates routes/menu by capabilities (`read`, `frontwindow`, `admin`) instead of assuming any authenticated user can access everything.
  - Adds mutation authorization guard on `/api/v1/ocie/complete-issue` so visitor-only users are blocked with `403`.
  - Extends unit + API tests to prove allowed/denied role behavior.

* <2026-02-19 Thu>
- [X] We have disabled several smoke tests. You will see that the user story, TechDebt, has a child ticket about this. We basically skipped a bunch of tests and added comments in the last week to keep things moving. These tests are basically failing because of fiddly stuff in the UI and it's kind of a failure mode for these smoke tests, which are really full end-to-end tests. that take a long time to run and so it's extremely expensive to try and yfix them when you have some modal that keeps falling over or whatever. To that end, I actually wonder if the smart approach might be to write a plain English description of the business process they're testing, you know, ha effectively manual testing instructions you would give a human as a block comment and then delete the test entirely and then start anew in each case. And we could run through them one at a time in this way. Just as additional context, it's really worth understanding that the test loop for these E2E tests is really slow. And the brittleness of the UI end of the testing has claimed many LLM attempts. It seems to be kind of a large language model trap to try and tweak. assertions around manipulating the UI and selecting the right elements and all that stuff. I've literally had runs that took overnight to fail to fix a single test because the LLM just got stuck in this kind of ant vortex trying to fix UI selectors And it's such a fucking waste of time because actually the brittleness isn't that important. You know, if a UI modal isn't where we expect it to be, then well, part of me just thinks it might be quicker to get a natural language description of what the test was intended to do without the specifics of the UI necessarily front and center of all that, although of course you want a reasonable minimum of UI so it's intelligible to someone new coming onto the task and then task it out and get it written. Because writing from scratch is quite often easier for large language models than fixing these kinds of tests, it turns out.

* <2026-01-07 Wed>
- [X] Make 90 min meeting for discussing db contraints with jk and cl
- [X] Deploy..? (Don't forget mobile)
- [X] Part 2 of ticket I started on - 27812, Joe added today


We had a bit of back and forth about what the task even was for that part 2 for 27812. Joe followed up with a message to me.

""""
The Problem
Workflow completion and document generation must be atomic. The document serves as the official proof (outside the system) that a workflow was completed. If data changes persist without the associated document, we have an incomplete audit trail.

Current risk: If a user refreshes mid-flow, data commits but the document is never generated—leaving no external record of the transaction.

---

The Requirement

One of the following must be true:

  1. Both succeed together — Data changes and document generation complete as a single atomic operation
  2. Both fail together — If either fails, roll back the other
  3. Recoverable — If data changes complete without the document, provide a way to generate the document retroactively (e.g., from a transaction log or "pending documents" queue)

---

One-liner version

Every completed workflow must have an accessible document; either make data + document atomic, or provide a mechanism to regenerate documents for completed transactions.
""""

In the initial investigation we found:

"""
● Investigation: Temporal Transaction Bundling (Ticket #27812, Part 1)

Question: If a user cancels at step 3 of 3 in the Issue Out workflow, do steps 1 and 2 le
ave committed data behind? Are all steps bundled in one transaction?

    ---
How the UI Workflow Works

| Step | Action                      | Data Written                                              |
|------|-----------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------|
| 1    | Select customer             | UI state only                                             |
| 2    | Add items to cart           | asset_reservation entities (temporary holds)              |
| 3    | Capture signature           | Held in memory                                            |
| 4    | Click "Complete Issue"      | Temporal workflow starts → permanent records created      |

Cart reservations are temporary guards, not business data. They prevent race conditions (
two clerks grabbing the same item) but are soft–deleted whether the user completes or aband
ons:

    UPDATE public.entities
    SET deleted_at = NOW()
    WHERE entity_type = 'asset_reservation'

    ---
When Does Temporal Get Involved?

Temporal only kicks in when the user clicks "Complete Issue." At that point, the ocieComp
leteIssueWorkflow runs and creates:

  - Hand receipt entities
  - Asset status updates
  - Transaction log entries

Before that button is clicked, no permanent business records exist.

    ---
Answer

No, steps 1 and 2 do not leave committed data if the user cancels at step 3.

The UI steps are preparation — they don't write permanent records. The reservations are t
emporary and cleaned up regardless of outcome. From a data perspective, the "transaction" o
nly happens when the user clicks Complete, and Temporal handles that as a single logical op
eration.
"""

I replied:
"""
Starting to question the requirement in my head a little. At the moment, we're treating the PDF like it's the authoritative record, when actually it's just a rendering. The transaction data is the source of truth and the PDF is derived from it. So generation can happen at transaction time, or on first access, or whenever. It doesn't need to be atomic with completion because it flows from data that's already committed.
"""

And Kevin replied to me:
"""
I'm in agreement that the document generation is secondary and only a point in time rendering. The current modal popup is confusing to me. I would expect to complete the transaction. then have an option to generate the document post transaction.
"""

* <2025-12-23 Tue>

> caffeinate -dmsu
What does it do in plain English?

⏺ caffeinate -dmsu is a macOS command that keeps your Mac awake by preventing various types of sleep:

  - -d — Prevents the display from sleeping
  - -m — Prevents the disk from idle sleeping
  - -s — Prevents the system from sleeping (when on AC power)
  - -u — Simulates user activity (like moving the mouse)

  In plain English: "Keep my Mac completely awake — don't let the screen turn off, don't let the disk spin down, don't let the system sleep, and act like I'm actively using it."

  It runs until you stop it with Ctrl+C or close the terminal.

> I'm on a MacBook which I can shut and I see the screen goes off when I do this although I believe
it doesn't like fully lock or stop running. Is it damaging to the hardware for me to do this? This.
I'm basically SSHing in to do stuff away from my desk, and sometimes I might leave it on for weeks
like that.

⏺ Running a MacBook with the lid closed is called clamshell mode — it's officially supported by Apple and not inherently damaging. But there are a few things to be aware of:

  Heat dissipation
  - MacBooks vent some heat through the keyboard area, so closed-lid operation runs slightly warmer
  - The fans will compensate, but ensure the laptop is on a hard, flat surface (not a pillow or blanket) for proper airflow
  - Weeks of use is fine — many people run them as headless servers

  Battery health
  - Keeping it plugged in 24/7 for weeks can contribute to battery wear over time
  - Modern macOS (Ventura+) has "Optimized Battery Charging" that helps mitigate this
  - You can also enable "Battery Health Management" in System Settings → Battery → Battery Health

  Practical tips for long-term closed-lid use
  - Keep it plugged into power (required for clamshell mode)
  - Elevate it slightly or use a stand for better airflow
  - Check Activity Monitor occasionally via SSH (top or htop) to make sure nothing is pegging the CPU and generating excess heat
  - Consider setting a reasonable auto-sleep timeout as a fallback if you forget to run caffeinate

  Bottom line: You're fine. This is a normal use case and won't damage your hardware if you keep it ventilated and plugged in.

> It sounds like I'm safe then.

⏺ Yep, you're good. Happy SSHing.

* <2025-12-05 Fri>

Note to self, the final PR I'm working on on Friday is all about having requests from the front end. go to the same route so that the front end doesn't have to know about the back end topology. Initially, I thought I would have everything go via the Actions API, but I realized that actually proxying and brokering is just fine too. So in fact, although one or two routes might have already been brokered by the Actions API, I think this was actually the wrong approach. And I'm instead swinging around now to having some of the routes proxied to Postgrest and the rest going to the Actions API. The idea is that the front end should end up with only a single route that it's hitting. while some middle layer decides which way requests should travel once they hit the back end. Whether they go to the Actions API or PostgreST isn't something the front end needs to know, but that also isn't necessarily a good reason to have the Actions API act as broker for everything.
The PR is already up in draft form and I've left Claude Code working on it in 'vterm-frontend-to-use-actions-api'
It would be worth stress testing the idea on Monday, just to make sure that it isn't silly to proxy rather than using the Actions API as middleman.
Also, Chris has a huge PR for the mobile app, which will probably be affected by this change, so worth checking in with him.

  - [X] Prompt: We need to add a mocked email notification that triggers whenever we complete issuing kit to a service member. To ensure we capture this event reliably across all write paths (PostgREST and the API), please implement a Transactional Outbox pattern: create a database trigger that automatically inserts a 'notification task' into a queue table within the same transaction as the kit issue. Then, configure a simple Temporal workflow to poll this table every few seconds and execute the (initially mocked) email sending logic. This approach guarantees 100% data consistency—if the kit is issued, the notification is queued—while keeping our API stateless and unblocked. I should add that this is the first time we are sending emails across this project, and so you could think of this as the inaugural implementation of something that will probably end up being broader. So this is like an example use case, and we're almost just mocking things out to show how it would work in this case, with a view to expanding it to other use cases later. By the way, one thing I'm unsure about is whether or not we already have some kind of outbox baked into the Postgres side of the house. Like, I have a vague memory that we might have put something in but kept it dormant, but I could just be plain wrong. It's probably worth noting that we basically want all database stuff to go through PostgreST. We're sort of using it as the interface, you see. You'll notice there are existing patterns around RPCs, views. And so on, as well as migrations.
  - [X] pg-mem integration tests would be super valuable, open q of whether we can have some kind of harness that spins up postgrest? Or use pglite? Whatever is least surprising, proven for the use case of integration tests.

http://localhost:8000/api/documents/b7954445-8ab0-4ec0-893c-7ed79d51c569

Work item detail:

ticket number, title
27304, Serve PDFs via URL
  In Equip, add a “Document” entity that stores the document URL and links to the related Transaction. Update the current flow so that when Equip requests a document to be generated, it saves the returned URL in this entity and the front end opens the PDF by navigating to that URL (new tab or in-app viewer) instead of constructing a blob or doing last-moment conversion. Keep existing view/download behavior but drive it entirely from the stored URL; if the URL is signed or time-limited, pass it through unchanged and show a clear error state if it’s invalid or expired. Include minimal metadata on the entity (type, filename, created/updated timestamps) to support the UI and auditing.

The goal is to make things a little closer to an object storage production environment setup, accepting that there's no object storage just yet.

- [X] Release to Demo
- [ ] Update deployment script to include all inclusions since last release branch (branches take the form 'release/n.n.n', so it's easy for you to check the commit messages since the last). Obviously the summary would be a bullet list of plain english sentences - one per feature. We do release branches to staging on a wednesday, so it'd just be for releases to staging. It should be skippable, Because you can imagine that we might deploy a release branch the first time with the notes generated, but then want to restart the deployment because of some fuck-up. with HTTP requests or something or if perhaps you know we're merging fixes as we spot issues in staging So, we don't want to create a new set of notes every time we deploy the release to staging. We just want to give people the option to do it and make it skippable. So, the opening steps in the script, I think, do something like: you know, they ask. which branch you want to deploy, which environment you want to deploy it to, and whether you're sure you want to go ahead with deleting the cluster and all that stuff. And we basically want, I guess, a third step that offers to make Release notes, and it only shows up if you're deploying a release branch to staging, if you see what I mean. And it's skippable. And it effectively hits an LLM API and generates release notes using a prompt that we will create together. And then presents the output to the user, asking them etc they want to accept it or Have them regenerated, and it makes clear that the notes are saved to a file in a given directory in the repo, so the user can edit them. This is gitignored This means that the user can regenerate them if they're feeling lazy, or they can just approve and edit in place while the script runs. And the script will then run. And when the deployment is successful to staging with the release branch, after the user has approved and generated a file, that file will then be sent with a webhook. like we do for other stuff. So the completed webhook will get sent as always, but we'll also send another webhook that sends the Release notes to an unconfirmed location. We'll figure that stuff out later. Things for us to do include writing a prompt which will include a template. We'll probably keep the template as a standalone file that is tracked by Git and lives in the deployments subdirectory somewhere. Like alongside the script, and that way we can include that file in the prompt. But it'll be a very simple format, you know, a simple bullet list, making clear it's Release notes for the given release version. And the prompt that presents that file will include some stuff about How the style should be very simple. Use plain English single sentence Per feature, you know, maybe two sentences by exception if things really deserve it, and written for a non-technical audience since the customer Isn't composed of software engineers, although they will be interested in what we've been up to. It's just worth noting quickly that When I create a release branch, Azure DevOps will have a list of work items associated with it because we have branch rules in Azure that force devs to associate each branch with at least one work item. This actually leads me towards wondering whether using the Azure MCP might be a good way to get some context around a release, since if you can see the release branch is associated to such and such Work items, then you can very easily infer what's getting pushed out. Of course, the trouble is that the Codex is the truth for a release, since a PR for a work item doesn't imply that the work item is done. And even if you can figure out That a work item is done because it's no longer listed as new or active or whatever, as its status It's still possible that a PR related to a work item is actually a fix and the feature is already deployed last week or whatever, which would lead to An LLM producing misleading release notes unless given broader context. So I sort of feel like taking a greedy approach and getting the list of work items and their descriptions and titles and all that shit and what state they're in. to support the prompt, but then still have LLM read the commits so that we know what's actually being deployed. This will mean that the prompt will be quite long. I'm on the fence about whether the LLM should be reading code or not. But at the very least, commit titles and descriptions should go into the prompt. Okay, I have a Codex command that would do the trick. Prompt to have Codex CLI retrieve a list of ticket titles / descriptions for a release: `codex exec --model gpt-5-codex --config model_reasoning_effort="high" --skip-git-repo-check "WITHOUT COMMENT: Use the Azure DevOps MCP to list all work item titles, descriptions, and statuses affected by the merge of branch release/0.1.2 into main. To do this, start by finding the completed pull request for the merge to identify its ID and completion time. Then, instead of inspecting the technical merge commit, perform a commit search within a tight time window around the PR's completion. Use the includeWorkItems flag to find the specific commit generated by the PR completion that aggregates all the linked work item IDs. Be aware this may be a separate commit from the primary merge commit. Finally, fetch the details for those work item IDs in batches and format the result as a markdown table."` Where in that case the release branch is obviously a variable. So I guess we would have the script ask for the version number and the user would just enter '0.1.2' or whatever into the deployment script prompt. So you can imagine that if the deployment script is told it's deploying a release branch to staging, it asks the user whether they would like to generate release notes. informing them that this will take a few minutes and will trigger Codex to suck down the relevant Work item titles, descriptions, and statuses before then having Codex Write up some release notes based on the combination of the Work item details and the commits made since the last release. If skipped, it we'll just crack on with asking the final are you sure question for the deployment. But if the user agrees to go ahead, then a series Codex steps will take place. And that will be okay. I'm kinda guessing that we can do everything Codex using the high model, if I'm honest with you. Like, you know, the output of that first script. Could well be the kind of thing that we provide along with A brief to the next exec instance Codex And that might get us most of the way there, honestly. You know, tell it to write to a file. Oh, yeah, and then when the Whole shebang is finished. We present the release notes to the user. And ask whether they are happy to proceed. And make clear to them that they can. Edit the release notes file in place and that it will be sent off to the customer (eQuip) via a web web hook when the deployment successfully completes.

- [X] Look into moving smaller workflows from temporal to Fastify. The fly in the ointment is that some of these are very clearly going to want to become durable workflows as we build out the app. So, for instance, you know, completing an order or whatever is probably going to be part of a much larger workflow, but scanning someone's badge, for example, instance isn't we're not really going to care about considering that a durable workflow and so temporal workers are probably overhead in that case. When we started this project we were told to use fission functions for small atomic bits of work. The overhead of keeping fission led us to setting up temporal workers as a place to house that logic until we truly needed Something extremely low latency. In the meantime, we've realized that temporal workers were probably not the right abstraction, and that the fact we have our Actions API Fastify service already means that there's an obvious place to put the stuff. Just in case now of not moving anything across that will soon enough become a Temporal concern.

Like, I don't think there's any way of rolling back when anything goes awry. How to do this? Postgresql is one service amongst like 40.  Is that it for now WRT state storage? In which case, how to manage this? most things go in via either Temporal or Postgrest.  Maybe that's all to worry about. But need to be sure first.  I guess I'm a little anxious because I'm used to working with a simple UI - BE - DB model (e.g. Laravel). But this is a distributed system that leaves open questions about whether state is going to be mismatched when rolled back, Since if state is scattered across lots of services, then rolling back is much more complicated than a simple Postgres transaction.

- [X] Task: rework Transaction Logs to be Asset Logs plus Transactions. Currently we log per asset in transaction (as in when we issue out 3 assets, we record 3x Transaction Logs in the db, one per asset for that transaction). We want to change this approach.  For each real-world transaction (for now currently just 'issue out', but will cover other types in future), we'd like a single Transaction entity created, and then for each asset in it we make an Asset Transaction related to that Transaction. So one Transaction to many Asset Transactions for each real-world issue out. We do already have a 'transaction logs' page, might be called 'document register log', I forget. It displays thing on a 'line per asset' basis by design, as customer asked for this, which is what led us to current data model; so we want to preserve this presentation but move the data model to the new proposed shape. So, straining the point, we have Assets. Asset Transactions will be introduced.  Transactions will be introduced. Transaction Logs were always kinda a misnomer because each entry ultimately relates to *both* assets rather than the real-world transaction they're part of, but whatever, multiple TLs per real-world t was always misleading.
- [X] Not to be a pain in the arse, but I think we should call Transaction Logs 'Transactions'. Since it's a distinction without a difference anyway - it's a database representation of a real-world transaction, so don't need word 'log' imo. So that way we have asset transactions on the one hand and transactions on the other. The suffix logs adds zero value as far as I can tell.
- [X] With regards to migrations, let's fold the change into the existing one. This is a prototype app that's still in the demo stage, and so there's nothing wholly about the existing data. We basically reseed every time we build. And so editing the migration that's already there might be cleaner when we think about future changes and so on. Just having it in one file, I think, is a lot better.

- [ ] Run through acceptance tests
Acceptance Tests*
Quick acceptance checklist (use this to verify end-to-end)
	•	Extend due date
	•	For an active, assigned THR, “Update → Extend due date” defaults to today + 90d.
	•	Cannot select a past date (UI + API).
	•	Saving updates the THR’s valid_to, grid reflects new date, reporting reflects within expected SLA.
	•	A log/audit record exists with actor, timestamp, old_date, new_date.
	•	Convert THR→PHR
	•	For a BOI item: conversion is allowed (no approval prompt or at least not required), valid_to cleared, due dates removed, log entry created.
	•	For a non-BOI item: dialog asks “Has this been approved?”
– Yes → conversion succeeds + log entry with approved=true (and ideally a free-text reference for memo/email).
– No → blocked; no mutation; clear error message.
	•	API enforces the same rules independent of UI.
	•	Guardrails
	•	Inactive/unassigned/closed rows do not expose the “Update” action (and API rejects attempts).
	•	Tests cover success + failure for both flows, including non-BOI detection.

*ROI & Activation* ?? Group 1<>

Muhammed Asmal (AdaptIT)
We implemented an AI intiative. We honed in on one ROI aspect. Copilot effectively 5x developers.  We assessed our product base - for 70%, copilot could be used to improve or rewrite.  We felt it was about 3 hour improvement per week for each developer, adding up to 18 weeks per year per developer; translating to revenue, $200k efficiency gain. The cost is about $1.8k. We've been able to monitor adoption within teams using Copilot admin panel. We can see adoption is going up. We're moving into the testing stage of the Enablement materials, 5/10, in Module 1. We've got 7 cloud products that will benefit from this. We're also starting to look at Design, 7/10, in Module 2.  We don't have a separate design team. PMs design stuff with teams. We've fed in design principles as plain text to copilot which does actually stick to them pretty well.  It's good as a start point, saves a lot of time.  We also do a lot of regulatory compliance, checking whether things are high risk / low risk audits. The same requirements passed to an AI, effectively made a form that is a ? flow chart for assessing risk.  Next we want to gain efficiency in assessing tenders. We want to upload an existing pdf, convert to word, answer questions, highlight things needed review in orange, then pass over to tender team.
So basically project-based, ROI downstream of money saved by projects that wouldn't otherwise exist, if not for AI.
Code coverage springs to mind.

Thapelo Mokole (AdaptIT)
Using Amazon Q. We maintain a 'maintainability index' using a plugin in Visual Studio. Cyclomatic complexity, lines of code, Halstead volume etc. We run code with poor metricks through Amazon Q using the 'Optimise' button in VSCode UI. Obviously requires testing as we do want to ensure it works after altering. Quick live demo on this. Very legible to developers, pulls code down into much more maintainable form.

Kevin Bradley
We did a cross-Omegro tech stack complexity assessment with Yonder last year.  The idea was that we'd repeat the assessment every quarter to see which way things are trending. Hoping that we'll drive towards ROI measures so that we can carry this back to the business.

Richard Howes
Replatforming example. 25 year old codebase. Challenge is that, after that long, you don't know how users are using it after. And replatforms tend to take too long. Strangler fig pattern, tried to make UI indistinguishable. Probably sped up by 4x - 1 month of work in 1 week. ROI plan fuzzy because been AI-first for over a year already, so hard to separate new practices.
Some resistance initially when trying to get peopl eonboard

Nico Von Ronge
We make available to all developers. Early morning sessions - 45 mins 3x weekly, with agenda set weeks out. Everyone joins, try lots of things, hacking, learning, growing, more about learning than the task itself. We converted many HTML to bootstrap, for instance, then started over - where the exercise is the point.

Muhammed Asmal
We'd love to get agents into Sharepoint, but governance / IT questions have prevented this so far; similar for deploying into MS Teams. From the user perspective, people are happy, but enablement from IT teams is slow.


* <2025-09-17 Wed>

*ROI & Activation* /w Formica(? Polzer) Cohort

Johan Campagner (Servoy)
Many of us already using AI in SDLC for over a year already.  So how to measure.  I asked R&D team how are we using, what have we gained.  We enabled Github Copilot for everyone 6+ months ago, but most using things prior. When you scope to documentation, we think it saves 50% time. Same for testsing. AI very good at these things. But when diving deeply into existing code and working on small new features or bugs, it's smaller, closer to 20%.
Team was already using for a while. I can see in Github Copilot admin screen that they're using it. We're a lot busier with AI than before. Implementing our own tools like MCP servers, integrating langchain into our product etc, etc.

Simon Trostel (Intellior)
We did similar. We ask developers if they use AI to complete their ticket. So in Jira each ticket has 2 new fields - 'AI use' (y/n)  and 'story points saved through AI'; every developer has to fill these out to close a ticket. Seen numbers from 2-8 story points saved through the use of AI. It's subjective to each developer. We accept negative numbers for 'story points saved', but have yet to see anyone enter this. Key that the story points baseline is still 'without AI' so that we can track the difference. Decided to just do story points, not percentages, because our initial estimates use story points.

Richard Carney (?)
Slides - how we plan to use AI for ROI. We have two projects planned, an internal tool (immediate term) to reduce risk while building skills and allow fail-fast approach; if this works, we'll move to the larger project, starting a rewrite of a legacy system.  Internal tool will be a licensing tool; planning to use 'reference documents' (roughly speaking ADR-based approach) for shaping coding agent behaviour.  We want to measure ROI through demonstrating we can keep up same progress with fewer developers on legacy project.  The legacy system was written 3ish years ago by Saatman(?) to replatform the system; the project failed; so we have informed estimate about the number of developers and time required. No measurements on ROI planned for internal tool work, it's just about building internal conviction.

Polzer - also how is internal learnin gfor AI going to be promoted going forward now?

Simon Trostel
Slides on ROI; but also demonstrating some wins. Every developer has ChatGPT and a JetBrains AI license. We have 2x developers actively participating in the AI Academy, have completed the basic modules.  All developers in our team are already using AI in their daily work - research, architecture, etc in ChatGPT, then JetBrains for implementation, documenting etc.
We don't have a clear framework, set of rules, or best practices for now. So we are starting to think about how to build a framework to implement it into developer workflows. Every developer in my team is testing & evaluating AI on their own, and then presenting back to the team on a daily basis.  Lots of "trying stuff out", which is working well. We've put in a little bit of process around the use of JetBrains AI and ChatGPT, but otherwise letting developers explore. We use Crucible to do code reviews on our own work. Looking to measure bugs in system over time. Story points as a measure. 2 months of work in 5 days in one case for an authentication feature.
AI Code review in addition to human code review.  But I have feeling that the second (human) review isn't necessary any more. This is a feature on the JetBrains AI Ultimate license - $40 per head.

Sebastian Bachstein (Hypersoft)
Can share a success in getting from mock-ups to code.  Legacy mobile point of sale, still in use by thousands of our customers. Want to revise the interfaces.  So gave our product to a marketing team, who created some mock-ups to look more appropriate for IOS / Android.  One of our developers then took the mock-ups and worked with Claude Code to create a frontend. These are a good version of the mock-ups, taking a week. ROI supposedly over 50% time gain.

It's 3pm on the day of the implementation, and so far I've initiated six attempts.

The first was the initial proof of concept, with two follow-ups that I never bothered running. I then spent a day with the team, developed an implementation plan, and I'm now running attempts four, five, and six.

I essentially had successive GPT-5 Pro prompts where I guided the model from its initial, relatively complex implementation to something much more scrappy. I think it started off too complex, then over-adjusted, and the sixth attempt is actually the middle ground. So, attempt four is the most complex, five is the least complex, and six is the middle ground.



- [X] Pipeline steps are personified as agents
- [X] Human in the loop angle - specifically, checklist items have a button for a human to approve (approved by default) or overrule, with freetext reason for why (We will advertise that this feeds back as training data for future models when we present this. In reality, we're doing everything in memory at the moment for the hackathon.  There isn't necessarily anything to do on the back end, although of course, we want the front end to update as a result.
- [X] Work in Paul's rubrics from Teams chat.  Key to note that colour and code are no longer separate. They're different ways of showing the same thing. We aren't separating judgement from colour; crudely: score is confidence that we're good, so to speak, and colour reflects score - one and done.
- [X] Colour coding in UI
- [X] Make UI look nicer
- [X] Ability to filter by colour - 'show the reds' (not this wording but yswim)
- [X] Top line one sentence statement will still show initially, but will update (LLM call!) when The user submits their various evaluations for the checklist items.
- [X] Make "Contract data remains in-memory only. Re-upload to refresh the workspace." a comment, that is, don't show it in the UI. The same applies to other references to in-memory elements in the UI. This is for a hackathon, so we want to maintain the spirit of hiding workarounds, while making them clear in the codebase so they can be easily identified later. By the way, I suppose I'm referring to that broader principle. If you notice other things like this in the UI that you think are worth mentioning, please list them after you've made the change. In fact, thinking more broadly than just hiding things we're working on later, there's a sense that the UI is a little bit fussy at the moment. You've got the main heading, and then the fact that it's self-documenting is quite nice. Let's talk about that. After you give me the list, just tell me whether the vibe as it stands is about right. It feels a little bit busy to me at the moment, having those numbered items on the same row. I'm not sure how you'd show them in an elegant way otherwise, to be honest, and I don't want to change the styles just for that. I want things to look good, so maybe they are fine as they are, unless you see an easy way.
- [X] In the UI currently, we allow the user to give feedback on the checklist items. We have a form structure where the user is presented with LLM judgements on risk and, as a reviewer, can overrule things. The health assessment currently always shows "healthy," which doesn't match what comes from the back end. The back end can indicate "healthy," "needs attention," or "critical," and often will show one of those. However, at the moment, we always see "healthy" on the front end for the reviewer outcome button. Secondly, the flow is wrong at the moment. Could the reviewer outcome, perhaps, be removed altogether? So instead of "approved," "needs attention," "critical," actually, it's just "approved," right? The reviewer decision—those three buttons—can be removed, because it's approved by default unless changed.Since we've already filled out the fields using the LLM response and the health assessment fields, if you change them from their original state, we should show the text box and require that it is filled in before submission.Does that make sense? Currently, the form isn't coherent because, on the one hand, it always shows "healthy" even though that often isn't the answer provided by the back end. Although the colours do change depending on this, I'm guessing it's a relatively small tweak to fix. However, we don't want the notion of "approved by the user" presented as a button in the UI, because everything is approved by default until it’s changed. That should determine whether or not the required text field appears. Of course, the form should ensure that this field is filled out before it submits.

* <2025-09-16 Tue>
*Progress & Insights Call* Polzer cohort

Richard Carney (Saatman)
2 projects.  One for a product, one for internal tool. Internal tool is the smaller project that they are doing first.  To do with tracking licenses. Focuses in measured way on what they noticed in coding with AI was 'gotchas' - hallucinations, repetition, code not compiling etc - presenting them as tradeoffs, managed by providing code examples etc to prevent models flying off.  The team also front-loaded architectural considerations, because they could see that otherwise lots of design assumptions would be introduced by the models.  They created a 'reference impolementation' based on Clean Architecture (see Bob Martin).  RI details some default logic, CRUD handling, generic processes like that; the idea is they would have a solution developed in their preferred language with boilerplate etc.  So they end up approaching AI with their own decisions around libs / architecture / frameworks, plus WRT lots of the little decisions about the repo, validation etc that fan out as you grow the repo.  Most of the talk by RI is basically about up-front design stipulations, as per C±± / C# / .NET / etc culture.  So architecture / cross-cutting concerns defined up front.  This definition goes into a read-only repository.  LLM agents then use this as a starting point.  No actual deliverable to show for it all - basically talking about how they've done planning up front *in anticipation* of using models to build; so basically - "we are on the start-line for this vision of how to progress this initial project", rather than "here are concrete deliverables".  I suggested we want to express things in terms of ROI for the next call.

Cristophe Meyer CM (Four JS)
Briefing on use of enablement materials. We started quite late on this (8 Sep). Mix of languages.  Very positive re using AI for documentation, explaining portions of code, linting, finding & fixing simple issues. Team found that AI efficacy varied a bit depending on language, but nothing surprising. Some diffculties around unexpected modifications to files, but they see this as something to manage along the way, since the benefit feels worth it. Framing this as a team journey, figuring things out so they can go fast.
Also a sidenote about an unusual language not well-represented in the training data - GENERO language, their Andej, we have an LLM to work.internal lang. Did some fine-tuning for specific objectives for working with the model (completion, commenting, description, etc).  A few lessons along the way about how to chuck code in sensible ways when feeding the model.  Time intensive: setting up examples, taste-testing results, adjusting etc.  They did this on their own metal, but slow; then did on AWS and was quicker; cost still a factor, but actually pretty low - 50-100 euros.

Konstantin Dombrowski KD (Hypersoft)
External developer created a chatbot on 'botpress' - an external tool for creating chatbots. Wanted to have it use documentation. Found CustomGPTs worked better in the end. KD then talks through steps taken with the project, not talking about team use of enablement materials.
When pressed - employees at various levels of progress through the enablement materials, some feedback re videos in EMs being too long, though otherwise those enagaging are progressing - except feeling that not everyone progressing, as at least one is 'too busy with a project'.  KD at least has been actively mentoring on individual basis

For catching up on Temporal work for eQuip.

The following summarises where I got to.

Pretty much ready to create PR2 for the [[/Users/robertkirby/g/eQuip%20USASOC/design/implementation-plan/temporal-workflow-engine.md][implementation plan]].

But still investigating the following (useful as a prompt):

"""
Don't edit anything. Just investigate

Summary of the issue under investigation
	•	Question: Should the Temporal Web UI be available on http://localhost:8082 when the environment is running?
	•	Docs vs. config:
	•	Environment docs list Tilt UI (10350), Kubernetes Dashboard (8443 via port-forward), Goldilocks (8081), PostgREST (3001), and Keycloak/Grafana/Prometheus via Tilt—no mention of Temporal.
	•	Project files indicate Temporal UI is intended on port 8082:
	•	design/implementation-plan/temporal-workflow-engine.md – references 8082 (multiple mentions).

Thabo Mogaswa TM (AdaptIT)
Ream of demos - figma design to figma MCP into Q Developer.

So used Q to analyse the code, expose issues, suggest ways forward.  [Shares screen...] Shows VS Code. But using Oracle extension.  Allowed them to get all the information they wanted. The code goes into Q Devloper, leads to an expected output via Q (Sonnet 4). "We link VSCode to the Oracle database to explain the current process.  Easily. It picks up issues in future etc. Database to JSON, which developer can then work against it. [Demonstrates a prompt:] highlights code, opens right click menu, sends to Q developer, adds a prompt.  Basically stripping data from HTML to make JSON output. Live edits are made. You can then review the migrated code." [Quotes a bit janky there haha]
I was really impressed with the demo. They have this going for 600ish files and I reminded them that this would be a great opportunity for the next [ROI] meeting.
Lindokuhle Thusini LT (AdaptIT, SWE) Figma designs to code.  MCP server for Figma to suck things down - "to expand the reach of AI". Q developer in VSCode. "Create an angular component for the currently selected Figma tree", where SWE (LT) has selected frame in Figma web UI - this the prompt in VSCode. It pulls down the frame via the Figma MCP, gives it to Q Devloper in VScode (Sonnet 4), and an initial version of the layout is created. Some follow-up prompts. Then a specific prompt for a dynamic table. "There is sucha component, just give me a plan, don't code yet."
"In the end, I didn't write any CSS code. And it gave me this [shows good screen]; obviously I had to prompt & guide it along the way. The results are very impressive. A page like this, when I write from scratch might take a day, but with this workflow with MCP + Q it took 10 minutes."
Kevin Bradley asks: "How much of this was from the course, how much were you dong already?"
TM: We'd already been doing this but not with Q.  Basically using Office 365 ChatGPT but manually copy & pasting. So people knew about it, but weren't using Q & MCP just yet. ROI is so clear now.

Debbie Holden DH (Gaina Software, senior SWE, Belfast).  Replatforming 30yo Oracle forms platform. Want to move to web-based platform.
Tiago Klauck TK (Gaina, SWE).  We used a custom GPT to help with shared components across the app. This improved performance of the agents. Using JetBrains / Q.  Used markdown files with coding standards to improve behaviour of the models.  We are converting those Oracle forms into XML for Amazon Q to read so it can create the modules for it to create a page for our chosen tech stack for the web. A MD file per page we wish to create, based on a template - Amazon Q creates the MD file from the template.  Basically an implementation plan. These then form instructions for Amazon Q to follow when implementing. This is surprisingly quick. Want later to hook up more MCPs for Q - git, PR merges.  Also looking into documentation and so on.
DH: 2k forms.  Going to reduce to 500. Moving to C# and .net

Nico Von Ronge NVR (AdaptIT). 2 use cases. 1 to track our usage on AI - are they copying, accepting etc. We wrote a tool ourself that connects to github and pulls the data into a dashboard. So e.g. since 11 Aug 37% of code suggestions accepted, 1950 chats, 129 led to copy & pastes etc. Number of active & of engaged users. 2 was security within GitHub. We scanned our codebase and found ~40 'critical' issues, all solved using AI, with no hands-on changes.  40 to 0. Had built up over 6 months. Many were HTML sanitisation.  We also switched on Q for code reviews - demos automated comments in GitHub on an existing PR. Then an additional initiative.  We investing in an automated AI QA tool named app.reflect.com - it has AI record a human's manual steps and automates the steps taken. It records the actions, then clarifies ("do you want random actions here, or does it have to be those inputs?" etc).
Michael Brandt (MB) did you pay for the QA tool?
NVR it's by Smartware, integrates with Jira. So the entire development framework. Will share link in chat. It's paid.

Oleksii Halahan OH (IDEA Data Solutions, SWE). Shows a product, it converts parts of unstructured documents into structured data.  Showing an example document. The application was written with Copilot. Document on left, results of processing on right. LLMs are used to extract some of the data, as the unstructured nature means that 'common sense' judgement is needed along the way.  Can parse tables and infer information from them. 'MDP-5000' documenet processing app. Python docling, which uses neural nets / OCR; then Ollama on their own infrastructure to create embeddings using their own self-hosted llama model; then Qwen3-32b via Groq for speed to extract data relevant to maintenance and generates suggestions on how to read the page; then kimi-k2 via Groq to generate question queries for multiple search - keyword searches, semantic embeddings searches etc; then kimi k2 via Groq that takes the query / search results and generates a final JSON structure with regular maintenance tasks.
Ollama on own infra because (a) it's fun and (b) eventually we want it all on our own infra for data security. 700 pages takes about 15 minutes. Iterating towards.  Took a week.
Niall Jack (NJ) very similar problem we've been grinding on, keep to talk with you, OH.

Application for specific domain (shipping industry).  So the prompt for the translating LLM has many domain-specific terms to keep things on track. Demonstrates translations basically via Amazon Q.  So the repo is the prompts / inputs / outputs and Amazon Q is the engine (using Sonnet 4).
Something we couldn't do ourselves - we'd have to hire someone. Next step to talk to people in the Shanghai office to fine-tune the prompt. But basically into smoothing / refining. £20k saved at least.

      - [X] We want to make sure that when there is a match, we always put a row into the CSV at the end of a research task. If we can't find a URL, then by all means we should update the discrepancies column so that there is a human readable explanation for why we have a row without a link supporting the decision to declare the company / tool pairing as a match. But in any event, we should never match a company and a tool and not then go on to add them to the CSV document. The failure to find an appropriate link is something we should document in the row rather than omitting the row.

      - [X] "Potential Discrepancy" column to go. Realistically here, we currently have a confidence column ("How confident you are about the information") in the CSV where you put like high, low, medium. What we actually want is for the LLM to reply with one of those three words and then we put a hyphen on the end and explain why in a few words. We can do all of that within the same column. Saves on having an extra column and it would also kind of be a superset of the discrepancy thing since we can prompt in such a way that encourages the LLM to explain what the discrepancy is that it sees. Such as EG... Well, I mean basically, you know, if the discrepancy reaches a certain threshold, it shouldn't even be in the CSV file I think, right? Since if we're going to provide a CSV showing a list of matches, if we can't demonstrate that something is indeed a match in any way whatsoever, I don't think we should show it. I guess some conditions we definitely want to hit. If the CSV creator, LLM stuff, can't find a supporting link at all, then I don't think we should show that entry in the CSV. And if... Actually, maybe that's the one situation where we do still want the discrepancy column thinking about it. Yeah, thinking about it, it's like, if there's no link, or if the link has no relevance at all, then we should definitely set confidence to low and explain why. But even in that case, it's like, is it truly a match? Probably not. But I guess you're doing it in the, how confident are you about the information column, rather than having an additional column for that purpose. Yeah, I think it's kind of okay, right? Maybe, you know, you have low confidence, and you start off with the word discrepancy, and then complete the sentence sort of thing. I don't know.

* <2025-08-08 Fri>
FOR MONDAY

Commit!

Things went well on Friday - The current diff on the researcher project simplifies down so that we just produce a CSV using a procedural workflow. Basically, ExaSearch followed by LLM CSV row picking followed by QC LLM call to make sure all the rows are good. And then we offer the file through the UI.

Today, you need to start by doing a large-scale search, maybe something like 20x20 or whatever, maybe even 50x50. We are really looking for memory leaks here. It's the sort of thing that GPT-5 might even be able to spot by sight.

In fact, the workflow might even be that we just do testing via the command line and have Claude Code or GPT-5 come up with tests for this and try to demonstrate that a memory leak can or does already exist.


Okay, once that's out of the way, I basically want to demonstrate that we can reliably get good results that match Nox expectations. Probably the Vancity stuff, 10x. And if you see the same results 10 times, then great.


At that stage we have a checkpoint that we definitely want to commit.

Then we are going to look to redesign towards Ian's vision of a flexible agent mode type application where the thing we are doing right now is simply a mode in the UI. Click a button to get the workflow that is currently on offer and to trigger the logic that's currently on offer. But actually the logic will be stripped out. We're going to end up having an agentic workflow. The prompt will be hidden behind a veil. So I think actually you would still have the same interface where you upload the two CSV files and we do checks on the formatting and all that kind of stuff. And then the key thing is that we have an agentic loop. I guess what we might do first is just introduce the idea of the mode. Right. Because once you have that, you can iterate on making it agentic where it is the app writ large. So basically for any workflow, you're going to accept natural language prompts. But in the case of the market intelligence research mode, you're actually going to not accept a prompt. You're just going to take the two files and the prompt will be injected behind the scenes. But then you're kicking off that agentic loop as described in my notes directory [[/Users/robertkirby/prompts/convert-mia-to-agentic-workflow.md][here]]. That file is a prompt to convert.  You might end up rewriting a little but it gives the starting position to get a loop that 'does the trick' WRT control flow to count as agentic. We'll probably need to bump the model to get the requisite quality of output. GPT-5-mini or GPT-5 or Sonnet 4.  But you see what I mean.  The goal is to first move to the mode abstraction, accepting that the front of house for the app will probably be a text field that accepts files, right? So it's kind of agnostic, but we expect text and potentially files as an output perhaps. And that the specific prompt for market intelligence will stipulate that we're just going to output such and such a CSV. And we're still feeding that same stuff to the same agent. It's just going to operate in a particular mode, right? Because we are going to do pairs-wise searches and CSV population and all that.

Yes, CSV rows can have unpopulated link columns.

The code explicitly handles this scenario at
/Users/robertkirby/g/researcher/src/a2a/services/csv-generator.service.ts:131:
sourceLink: primarySource?.url || ''

This happens when:
- No web sources are found during research
- Source extraction/parsing fails
- Research evidence comes from non-web sources
- All sources are filtered out as invalid

The system gracefully handles empty links by:
- Setting the sourceLink field to empty string
- Adjusting confidence to "Low - no supporting sources found"
- Still including the row with other valuable data (company, tool, product, confidence)

Test coverage at lines 185-227 of csv-generator.test.ts specifically validates this behavior with
empty source arrays.

It's a no brainer in terms of value.  We've got tasks we know would take us a week now taking a couple of hours.  Months -> week etc. Scaffolding is just so much quicker. * <2025-06-26 Thu>
The session was a good example of my stance on how training means frontloading doing: they *led* with a warmer.

There are no slides prior, the tables of 6ish people are asked to talk on this:

After that, a cadence of a practical task *every 10 mins max* - and probably every 5ish mins on average.

""""
Take 15 mins with your table, think of as many use cases for AI regarding the 3 below PS areas and prepare one slide to present your findings:
Process Improvements
Customer Deliverables
Predictive Analysis
""""

The room then hears about 30s from a nominated person from each table.

The suggestions were basically fine.  Several tables used ChatGPT to get a list of candidate suggestions.

For the first 20 minutes, the people running the session basically didn't talk beyond setting up the initial task.

The team running the session  *then* present a slide named 'our ideas' - i.e. they had skin in the game for the warmer task, as they themselves were to present their own crack at the challenge.

The follow-up suggestions included some prompt suggestions, and these were basically fine.




Initial broad terms ROI slide (very broad, less engaging, but only hovered there for 20s).
Is actually a preamble to 'homework slide' on same topic immediately after - the payload is the exercise, not someone talking.  This idea introduced right away.
"Each VBU [now] take 5 mins to create experimentation ideas with simple ideas"
"We will reconvene Sep 15th to talk about your experiments"

It's been less than 5 mins since last exercise and tables are already invited to come up with ideas, implicit that each tables will feed back to the room shortly.
[My table - immediately thinking about customer onboarding documentation, how it might even be used to signal to customers, improve brand by seeming modern, etc.]
(Engagement a little lower on this bit, kind of became tables setting world to rights)
We didn't feed back, but it didn't matter because the ambiguity meant we prepared as if we would.


Then it looked like 'AI track' part ended, but sharing the rest anyway.
And then Dave Corbett gives a standalone 15ish min presentation on concept of quadrants, causes for low PS margins etc..?
Felt totally disconnected from session to this point, instead part of the 'general PS materials' track.
Effectively an intro to how Volaris measures success.
Very light touch, image-heavy slides, one hook per slide from speaker.
'Plug in into ChatGPT' as an aside, but basically entirely about PS metrics, not AI.
A basic 2 min exercise about 10 mins in.
Then 10 mins more slides with a 15ish min group discussion (room-level, one voice at a time). Expansive / unrushed, following threads suggested by the audience.

* <2025-05-30 Fri>
******FOR MONDAY********

*Take note of the below, but I've already started work on it*
*See the plan file - can point Amp at it:*
/Users/robertkirby/g/ssp-project/agent-notes/generify-further-using-input-schemas.org


See the most recent AI Studio Chat. I shared a screengrab in the group chat with Ian & Chris, although I still have it open in the browser too.

I want to make the agent card dynamic (DB, not yml file) and I want to remove domain specific language from the UI and Python server. Anything domain specific can live in the agent card and therefore in the database.

I also want to hook up the A2A server to the MCP backend using SSE to talk to it.  It will be worth stopping to think whether we should do both of these things in a single Gemini prompt since `make copy` / `make copy-mcp` from ~/g/ssp-project/ will load everything we need into the clipboard.

It might well be the case that the MCP stuff actually needs to be stipulated in the Agent card, since ultimately that is domain specific. So perhaps the critical path is to get things hooked up to the MCP server first.

he main areas where domain-specific language/logic still exists outside the "configurable objects" are:
Backend (claims-a2a/app/skill_executor.py):
The _execute_insurance_skill function and its helpers (_execute_create_claim_skill, _execute_search_claims_skill, _execute_get_claim_skill) contain Python code that explicitly understands "claims," "policy numbers," how to generate CLM... IDs, and how to structure/query the claim data stored in TaskSQL.data.
The success message templates in agent_config.yaml for these insurance skills (e.g., Claim submitted for policy {input_policy_number}. Claim ID: {result_claim_id}) are domain-specific (which is fine as they are config), but the Python code populating the context for these templates (e.g., template_render_context["result_claim_id"] = claim_id) also has this domain knowledge.
Frontend (Universal-UI):
Screen Titles/Layout (ClaimsDemoScreen.tsx): The title "Insurance Claims Demo" and the tabs "Submit a claim" / "Search claims" are hardcoded. Ideally, these would be more generic or derived from the loaded AgentCard (e.g., agent name, skill names).
Result Rendering (SearchClaimsScreen.tsx): When displaying search results, the code directly accesses claim.claim_id, claim.policy_number, claim.incident_description, claim.status. A truly generic version would need a way to display arbitrary data from an artifact, perhaps guided by a display schema or by iterating over key-value pairs more abstractly. The same applies to displaying ClaimDetails.
Skill ID Checks: Code like agentCard?.skills.find((skill) => skill.id === 'create_claim') is looking for a specific, domain-related skill ID. A more generic UI might list available skills from the agent card and let the user choose, or be configured to target a specific skill type rather than ID.
How far are things?
The foundational plumbing for generic A2A communication, dynamic form rendering from schema, and configurable skill dispatch is mostly there (70-80% of the way for the core generic parts).
The insurance-specific skill implementations in Python are the most significant piece of domain-specific code that isn't just "configuration." To achieve the vision, these would need to be refactored. For example:
The create_claim, search_claims, get_claim logic would ideally live in actual external MCP tools. The current Python functions are effectively stubs for these tools, but they contain the domain logic.
Alternatively, if you wanted to keep some local execution generic, you'd need a "local function executor" skill type where the Python function to call and its argument mapping are defined in the config, and that function itself is more generic (e.g., a generic DB interaction tool that takes table and field names from config).
The frontend requires relatively minor changes to make titles, tabs, and result rendering more data-driven from the AgentCard and Artifact structures, rather than hardcoding for "claims."
You've successfully built the generic framework and then instantiated it with an insurance example. The next step towards the pure vision is to push the "insurance" part further out into the configuration or into external tools/services that the generic framework can call.

Proposed Ideal Architecture:
UI: (e.g., Swagger UI, a custom frontend) - Sends requests to the A2A Server.
A2A Server (Agent Server):
Receives requests adhering to the A2A JSON-RPC protocol.
Handles authentication, request parsing, and task management (tracking state like SUBMITTED, WORKING, COMPLETED).
Orchestrates work by calling MCPs. It translates A2A skill requests into one or more calls to appropriate MCPs.
Largely stateless regarding business logic execution, delegating that to MCPs.
Formats responses from MCPs back into A2A protocol.
MCPs (Model Context Protocol Servers):
Specialized services, each potentially focused on a specific domain or data model (e.g., a "Claims MCP", a "Policy MCP", an "LLM Interaction MCP").
Encapsulate the business logic and data access (CRUD operations) for their respective domains.
Expose an interface (perhaps also JSON-RPC, or gRPC, or REST) that the A2A Server can call.
Have direct access to the data layer (databases, external APIs).

http://claims-a2a-poc-volaris.australiasoutheast.azurecontainer.io:8000/health

Legal‑Doc PoC – Full Build Spec  (v 1.2 | tree‑structured TODO inside)
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Context
-------
Skunkworks team, green‑field repo, Azure‑only stack, licence to “just
build.”  You begin in an empty folder after `git init` **plus** a copy of
the `local.settings.json` shown below.  Assume common dev tools
( Azure CLI, Functions Core Tools, Poetry/Pipx ) may already be installed,
but include install steps for fresh boxes.

Business Glossary
-----------------
| VBU  | Volaris Business Unit (subsidiary)                               |
| A2A  | In‑house task‑queue manager (repo: *A2A‑Prototype*)              |
| MCP  | In‑house tool layer (repo: *MCP‑Prototype*)                      |
| EstateEdge / Phantom | Code‑names for the current legal‑doc product     |
| AlexandriaAI        | Parent platform repo holding canonical            |
|                     | `functions/core/local.settings.json`              |

local.settings.json  (seed copy)
--------------------------------

Tree‑Structured TODO
--------------------
- [ ] **Bootstrap environment**
  - [ ] Verify `az`, `func`, `poetry` are available; install if missing.
  - [ ] `az login` and set correct subscription.
  - [ ] `git init` new repo `legal‑doc‑task‑engine`.
  - [ ] Add `.gitignore`, `README.md`, MIT LICENSE.

- [ ] **Project skeleton**
  - [ ] Create directory tree (`src/`, `.github/`, `.devcontainer/`, etc.).
    - [ ] `src/api/` FastAPI app.
    - [ ] `src/ingestion/` Azure Function v4 BlobTrigger.
    - [ ] `src/ocr/` OCR utilities.
    - [ ] `src/extraction/` LLM prompts + ensemble logic.
    - [ ] `src/risk/` rule engine + `risk_rules.yaml`.
    - [ ] `src/storage/` Cosmos+Blob wrappers.
    - [ ] `src/tests/` pytest suite.
  - [ ] Initialise Poetry; export to `requirements.txt`.

- [ ] **Azure resource provisioning**
  - [ ] Create resource group `rg-legal-doc-poc`.
  - [ ] Storage account `legaldocstore` + containers `raw`, `markdown`.
  - [ ] Cosmos DB serverless SQL (`legaldoc-cosmos`) + DB `contracts`
        + container `extracted`.
  - [ ] Azure OpenAI account `legaldoc-openai`; deploy three models:
    - [ ] `gpt-4o`
    - [ ] `gpt-4-turbo-2024-04-15`
    - [ ] `gpt-35-turbo-16k`
  - [ ] Key Vault `kv-legal-doc`; import secrets, connection strings.

- [ ] **Ingestion function**
  - [ ] Implement `blob_trigger.py` to react on upload to `raw/`.
  - [ ] Push basic metadata message onto Azure Queue for orchestrator.

- [ ] **OCR pipeline**
  - [ ] Detect text layer in PDFs; decide OCR vs direct extract.
  - [ ] Run Tesseract (or Azure Vision) per page.
  - [ ] Combine to single `.md` file in `markdown/`.

- [ ] **Extraction ensemble**
  - [ ] Write system + user prompts for key‑field JSON.
  - [ ] Fan‑out to three model deployments (async).
  - [ ] Majority‑vote reducer; tie‑break on token count.

- [ ] **Risk flagging**
  - [ ] Load `risk_rules.yaml` at startup.
  - [ ] Append `riskFlags` list to extraction JSON.

- [ ] **Persistence layer**
  - [ ] Upload Markdown blob.
  - [ ] Store extraction JSON (+ raw risk) in Cosmos container.

- [ ] **REST API**
  - [ ] FastAPI endpoints:
    - [ ] `POST /upload` (alt to direct blob drop).
    - [ ] `GET /contract/{id}` returns stored JSON.
  - [ ] Add OpenAPI docs (`/docs` route).

- [ ] **Testing & CI**
  - [ ] Fixtures: sample PDF, DOCX, 1998 photocopy scan.
  - [ ] `pytest` covering OCR, extraction, risk, API.
  - [ ] GitHub Actions:
    - [ ] On push: poetry install, `pytest -q`.
    - [ ] Optional: Docker build + push to ACR.

- [ ] **Containerisation & deployment**
  - [ ] Dockerfile (Python 3.11‑slim + poetry install).
  - [ ] `func azure functionapp publish` script.
  - [ ] README deploy section with `az` commands.

- [ ] **Optional niceties (v 1.x)**
  - [ ] Lightweight drag‑and‑drop HTML page hitting REST API.
  - [ ] Basic auth / JWT using `JWT_SECRET_KEY`.
  - [ ] Cosmos container for evaluation runs (`eval_runs`).

- [ ] **Eventual goals (track but do not block v1)**
  - [ ] Precision ≥ 90 % on Party/Jurisdiction/Date in benchmark set.
  - [ ] Processing cost ≤ US$5 / document.
  - [ ] 24 h SLA for 400 docs/week throughput.
  - [ ] WORM storage & field‑level encryption if compliance requires.
  - [ ] Integration with A2A/MCP repos.

Example of a done task
- [X] Resource group `rg-legal-doc-poc` created in East US.












Rob:
Are the docs to be manually uploaded by users?

Ian:
We can do the UI after we get the task engine going.
What I’m not sure is if we tie the ui up to the service directly or a proxy to expose a clean rest api

The task was set as follows:
"""
Transcript

Ian Reay (21:38):

The key elements of the use case are below:
	1.	Layers want to upload Word documents and PDFs. Some are low‑quality scans of old agreements, e.g. screenshots in PDF form.
	2.	Use the AI to “read off” the docs into Markdown so we can analyze and reason over them. We’d store both the translated versions (for auditing) and the originals in a database or blob storage.
	3.	Once we have the text, we’d want to:
	•	Extract key elements (e.g., parties’ names, enforcement location, dates).
	•	Assess risks (e.g., flag contracts governed by jurisdictions we struggle with—like California—or those with “favoured nation” clauses).
	4.	Store the extracted information too—these are the bits we’ll explain to the lawyers.
	5.	Build evals to measure accuracy: if you feed the same poor‑quality 1990s scan 100 times, how often does it pull the right data?
	6.	To boost accuracy, run the doc through multiple models and take majority‑vote (e.g. send to three models; if two agree, that wins).

It would be fascinating to see how far it gets with this.



Rob Kirby (21:45):

Are the docs to be manually uploaded by users?

Rob Kirby (21:45):

I think this will be disappointing with the current generation of models, just based on what founders have said in this space.

It’s ultimately just about beating the contractor in the eyes of VG assessors, which I accept—but go in expecting that the devil’s in the details of how we prompt, and that most of the work will be in crafting correct evals.

https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0DDS8jWqEPg

I.e., this is famously not a solved space, and many are running at it.

⸻

Ian Reay (21:48):

We can do the UI after we get the task engine going. 👍

What I’m not sure of is whether we tie the UI directly to the service or put a proxy in front to expose a clean REST API.

⸻

Rob Kirby (21:51):

And regarding the repos:
	•	A2A‑Prototype
	•	MCP‑Prototype
	•	A2A‑Researcher (I don’t have access to this one)

How do you see them fitting into the task currently? I understand you’re keen to see if MCP can help.

As templates? Or as tools?

⸻

Ian Reay (21:52):

Will fix when I get home in 15 minutes.

A2A is the task manager.

MCP can then give you access to additional tools.
A2A sits on top of MCP.

⸻

Rob Kirby (21:52):

Honestly tempted to roll something from scratch, keep it modular, and work them in when the time comes.

I’d like to get things actually up and running on Azure—and I’ll need the config/environment vars to do it. I’m guessing I could pillage from somewhere like:
AlexandriaAI/functions/core/local.settings.json

Implicitly, you’d want the “task engine” to be reusable, so there are hidden concerns I should avoid stepping on—like we saw with AlexandriaAI (where the immediate project is “EstateEdge”/Phantom, but there are longer‑term platform considerations). It’s worth thrashing those out.

If you don’t actually care about reusability, I’ll blast it out without worrying and pick up the MCP/A2A concerns (and those repos) later. Since we’re just proving the legal use case, a sufficiently modular approach can leave space for them.
"""

Robert Kirby [16/04/2025 21:53]
I would like to get things actually up and running with Azure, and that I’ll need config / environment vars to do it – I am guessing I could pillage from somewhere like:
AlexandriaAI/functions/core/local.settings.json

⸻

Robert Kirby [16/04/2025 21:56]
I suppose the point implicit here is that you would want the ‘task engine’ to be reusable, and so there’ll be hidden concerns I should avoid stepping on, as with AlexandriaAI – where on the one hand the immediate project is “EstateEdge” / Phantom, but in actuality there’s longer term empire building / platform considerations for the codebase to respect. It’s worth thrashing those out.

If you don’t actually care about the task engine being reusable, I’ll just blast it out without worrying, and pick up the MCP / A2A concerns (including those repos) when we feel they are needed. Since I’m conscious that we’re proving out the legal use case, and that a sufficiently modular approach can leave space for them.

Generated questions, am happy to make reasonable assumptions for them all, but floating in case any have non‑obvious answers.

There is always a slight tension between “just build a demo” and “build the real thing”, since in practise nobody ever expects you to throw things away unless you push hard for the option.
	1.	Are uploads solely manual via browser, or do we need batch/API‑driven ingestion (e‑mail drops, SharePoint, S‑FTP, etc.)?
	2.	Which file types do we expect: Word/PDF only, or also image formats (TIFF, JPEG)?
	3.	What’s the expected document volume (roughly how many docs per week)?
	4.	Do we control scanning hardware, or must we handle low‑quality scans (e.g. “wonky 1998 photocopier”) entirely in software?
	5.	If quality is too low, will re‑scanning be an option, or must all processing be automatic?
	6.	In which Azure region(s) must blobs live, and are there data‑residency constraints (e.g. UK‑only for GDPR)?
	7.	What are the retention/deletion policies for originals and Markdown versions?
	8.	Do we need legal‑hold or audit‑trail versions (e.g. WORM storage)?
	9.	Must we apply field‑level encryption or redaction for any PII or sensitive data the models emit?
	10.	Is there already a canonical schema (e.g. Party, Jurisdiction, EffectiveDate), or do we define v1 now?
	11.	How are risk heuristics defined: via a config table of jurisdictions/clauses, or fed in at runtime?
	12.	Do we have any labelled agreements to bootstrap evaluations, or must annotation be part of this project?
	13.	Which target metrics matter most (precision/recall thresholds, human‑time‑saved per doc, etc.)?
	14.	How large will the test corpus be for consistency evals (e.g. how many docs for 100× runs)?
	15.	Are there budget constraints on model calls (e.g. cost caps per doc or overall)?
	16.	Should our service expose the same interfaces A2A expects, or will A2A be adapted later?
	17.	Are there other internal consumers (reporting, BI, secondary UI) that need a clean REST API now?
	18.	Do we inherit secrets via local.settings.json, or is Azure Key Vault (or another store) mandated?
	19.	What’s the minimum demonstrable outcome (MVP) for the next steering‑group meeting?
	20.	Who can provision Azure resources/service principals, or do I get contributor rights?
	21.	What success criteria will signal that the legal use‑case is proven and ready for production?

⸻

Ian Reay [Yesterday 23:05]

each MCP and A2A would be its own repo

because it’s a pain to get all the infrastructure for secure coding setup














The key elements of the use case are below:

1) Lawyers want to upload word documents and pdfs. Some are of low quality and are basically screenshots of old agreements in pdf form for example.
2) Use LLMs via Azure OpenAI Service to "read off" the documents into a markdown version that we can then analyze and reason over them. We would want to store the translated documents for auditing as well as the original docs in a database or blob storage of some kind
3) Once we have the text of the document, we would then want to do things like
Extract out key elements from the documents. I can get you a list of items in the morning. But for initial testing think about things such as the names of the parties in the contract, the location the contract is being enforced, dates, etc.
Assess risks in the contract. Ask the AI to alert to cases where the contract is in a legal jurisdiction we struggle to do business with ( like california ) and favored nation clauses as a couple of examples.

4) Store his extracted information as well. These will be key elements we will want to explain to the lawyers.

5) We would want evals to udnerstand how accurate this process is. Ie if you send the same horrible doc with scans of 1990's contracts how many times of out of 100 will it extract the right information

6) A way to improve the accuracy might be to send this into multiple models and see if their resutls agree. If you send it into 3 models then the two who agree win-

Prompt to generate a work orders Laravel app for demoing SQL injection fix:
#+begin_quote
I want you to take full control. You can make tech choices, install dependencies correctly, run tests properly, run the code, set up environment variables, install anything that is required, and generally just act like a senior engineer who is in charge of the system. As a rule, I will approve everything, and I dislike being asked. I’d rather you just exhibit high agency and go for it.

Please create a Laravel web app, doing everything in a ‘boring’ and ‘by the book’ way. I want it all standard and predictable.

It’s a property management app — a landlord login portal.

It should present a login page, then a home page, and a menu of mostly dummy options, but with a button to ‘Create Work Order’. This should open a modal with some typical fields, which can be submitted and saved. The home page should display a list of previously created work orders.

Let’s have some feature tests, and let’s use SQLite in-memory for those so we can test end-to-end fast.
